    on Earth have a Spl itual “shadow” in this part of the Umbra.

    Umbra: The SpIrit worlds as a whole, encompassing the Penumbra and the 13 Umbral Realms. urrah: An insulting term for a werewolf who chooses to live too close to humanity.

    Prophecies of Shadow: The 10 visions brought to the Garou by Songs of Shadows, a mighty seer. Each vision corresponds to a tribe; one of them has already come to pass.

    War of Rage: The war the Garou fought against the other Fera. The ones they did not slaughter were driven into hiding, and most now hate and fear the werewolves.

    Realm, the: The physical world (as opposed to the Limbra).

    sept: A large community of werewolves, usually centered around a caern.

    Weaver: A member of the Triat; the spiritual force of order and stasis.

    Triat: The three spirits responsible tor keeping Wyld: A memberof the Triat; the spiritual force balance in the universe. of chaos and creation. tribe: One of 10 cultures of werewolves, each Wyrm: A member of the Triat; originally the bonded by a tribal totem and by ideology and — spiritual force of balance,the Wyrm has nowbecome shared history. a force of corruption and entropy.

    Triat: The three spirits responsible tor keeping balance in the universe.

    Filthy pagans, thought Pasta Oe.

    It wasa strange thousht for a werewolf but there it was. His tribemate, a wolfborn Ahroun called something like “Render of Spiders” straightened herself up and continued on her tirade about Christians. Sheseemed to feeltthat they were destructive and ultimately useless. Hasta Dei felt his hackles rising as his faith was insulted, but he bore it quietly, asking God's forgiveness each time a blasphemy escaped the Ahrounslips. Finally, she brought up the fall ofConstantinopleand how the Red Talons’ prophecy had foreseen it, and Hasta Dei — the StaffofGod — could bear no more. He stood up, drivingthe iron spike at the end of his stafFinto the ground hard enough that the werewolves assembled there jumped. “Constantinople fell, yes,” he said, the word strugslingto escape his clenched teeth, “but to what? Not Christianity, no.” “Then what?” A Ragabash would havequestioned Hasta Dei to test him. The Ahroun simply wanted an answer.

    “Tomoney,” hesnapped.“Morey.The humans will goon holy crusades,yes, but doso onlyfor profit. When the moneyran out, the crus a ttackeddersthe first thing they saw." The Ahroun snapped at a fly, the lupus equivalent, Hasta decided, of shrugging. “And so what ifmoney. did spur them,to sack the city? Christians take money every week, or so you tell us, StafFofGod. Ifthe Churchdesires money, then is it not as corrupt as the money itself?” | Hasta Dei smiled. The Ahroun might be born of wolf, but she thought like a university scholar, “The Church is corrupt. But tell me: IF a sept of Silver Fangs is corrupt, spoiled, fat and lazy, does that invalidatth e Litany? Does it tarnish Gaia? Or do those spoiled Garou instead do themselves diseredit by behaving thus and then calling themselves Garou?” Render of Spiders dtopped her head into her paws and considered this. The other Garou around looked at one another and murmured. Many of them had been Christian before their First Changes but had abandoned the faith because it didn’t seem to fit with what they could see and feel as werewolves. Hasta Dei disagreed, God’s Grace was all around them, ifthe Garou would simply see it and not be misled by the prophecies ofthe beasts. } i) e The Ahroun raised her head again. “So how did those crusaders break with their faith? What does their faith say?” Staff ofGod grinned. “Im rather slad you asked.”

    The children of the crescent moon are the the growing numbers of urban poor. Bone Gnawers Theurges, the mystic scholars and explorers. They have little time for nobility, either human or Garou. travel the spirit paths and learn secrets that other Gnawers also pay little mind to laws that go against auspices cannot understand. They protect against the commonsense. They havespread throughout Europe, magics of other supernatural beings. Most of them and along with the Warders,they even have caernsin know the secrets of healing as well. the midst of human settlements. Although most other The halt moon brings balance, and the Philodce x werewolves lox ik down upon them, the Bone Gnawers are the judges and laweivers i f the Garou. They can make up one of the most resourceful tribes. Rat looks command the spirits and enforce the will of Gaia, after this tribe. Without them, the hierarchy of the Garou would fall into chaos.     The room wasn't high, but she felt as though the people below were miles away, The sky was rapidly darkening — tonight would be doubly black, as no moon would shine, and the clouds would obscure what feeble illumination the stars could provide.

    Elizaveta sighed, She glanced over at her plate, empty but fora few chicken bones, and was shocked to find she was temptedto pick up the tiny scraps and shaw what tiny bit of meat might remain. This was not behavior becominga lady. Lonely as she was, she was also glad that no one could see her these last few weeks. Her 13th birthday had been the start of it, That night, she recalled, had also been without moon, and her womanly flow had beguntheverysameday. Shehad been terrified to see the blood, but just:the same, she had feltsomethingwake inside her. A hunger, shesupposed. Secretly, she felt[ it] might be desire for a man’s touch, as her nurse had so often described, but shewasn'tsure. All she knew was that it frightened her, and that when she had communicated her fearsto hermother, Elizaveta had been locked inthis room. Nowhere she remained. She started as she heard the howlsof wolves and the screams of horses. Perhaps one of the animals had gotten loosecommonand folkbeen werebrought convinceddown— that itaElizaveta’shappened familybefore,ve[Wolves] protected[ were] from[ commonplace] the beasts[ around] somehow.[ Blovice,] The young[but][the] noble didn’t know, but o eae comfortedwhen thy howled in the dark nights. The sound made herfeel as though all was right in the worl ¥ TheThe last: thing she expectedwas to see one leap through her window. night wasn't cold, so the window was not shuttered. The creature landed next to her, a massive, black-furred animal. It turned to her and sniffed. Elizaveta drew ina breath to scream, but felt a soft voice in her mind. “Do not cry out, child. | am not here to harm you.” quietly andThe gazed voice wasat the like wolf, a dreara wishinglover, for like the voice the kind totcontinue. seenIt did. in those fevered visions of late. She sat “Elizaveta, your family holds you here to keep you away from your true life. They knew and cherished their heritage once, but your[father][was] acowardwho felt himselfdamned when his sister Changed. | hope that you are made of stronger stuff.” ‘4 Thewolfstepped towardher,and Eli ot felther heart pounding,She looked down at her handsand saw that coarse black hair had sprung up from the backs. The wolf seemed to smile atherep “Let it come, little sister. You'll know the answers soon.” “What is happening?” Her voice was thick, as if her throat were full of blood. “You are becoming a woman,” answered the wolf. “But so much more. When you visit our sept in the high mountains, deep in the forestsyou will know freedom for the first time.” was the voEl i zavetace in her smiled mind.and relaxed, She thoughtpera this might be a dream,‘ so convincingly and natural “Then, of course,” said the. wolf, “we shallreturn you-to your rooms.” issue Elizaveta started, “What?" Hervoice was deepernow, and more ofa growl than a sound that: should from a woman's throat. / L as “I'm sorry, dear, butwe need you here. Your father made sehahorrid mess of your family's affairs, and we can't afford to let them know anything is wrong,” until The girl fell to her hands and knees, her body already contorting, the hunger she felt before increasing she was the howl, was the rage, was the wolf. She tried to speak, but onlygrowled, The voicein her head was still there, however. “Come, child ofThunder. Come and meet: your family. As | said, the answers are coming.”

    Character creation for Dark Ages: Werewolf follows much the same formar as for Dark Ages: Vampire. This chapter provides all the necessary information for creating werewolf characters, but the player might wish to reread Chapter Five of Dark Ages: Vampire for the basics.

    Garou of the 13th century generally come from different backgrounds than vampires caught in the War of Princes. A bit of a change of mindset is in order to build believable Dark Ages: Werewolf characters.

    Yoonne NrovenMoices sat cpossed-Legged on the ¢pound, concentratingon theax in front of her. Her younger sister-in-Fenris, an Ahroun called Sees-OnlyBlood, had asked her to awaken the spirit ofthe weapon. This normally wouldbe an easy task for the Theurge. Awakening weapons had become somethingof a specialty for her since her Rite of Passage had demanded that she perform the rite without really knowing how. Yet the ax sat inert in front of her She tried to tap out the rhythm that would coax the spirit into wakefulness, whistled a battle tune and even considered finding another werewolfto stage a mock duel. It was all for naught, she knew. A spirit. would not. wake unless it was addressed directly, and that required full concentration on the part 6fthe Garou. Yvonne had been able to give precious little her full concentration since her trip to Wales.

    She stood, disgusted, and left the ax there on theground for a moment. She untied the stripof leather holdingher hairbackand shook herthicklocks free. Thisis absurd, she thought. Not only is he Garou, but he's butaboy.Just outofhisRite ofPassage. Andhe’s half'a world away, not that it's a bad thing that he is. rc “What troubles you, Hidden-Voices?” Yvonne started, but recognized the voice. A tiny cuckoo-spirit sat on the.ax, looking quizzically up at her. She knew from experience that lyingto the harmless-lookingspiritwas unwise, but she sat down so as not to attractany other attention, “There is a man,” she began, and then stopped. “A Garou. A Fianna.” “You met him on your mission east?”

    Yvonne nodded, “He hasyet tojoina pack. Hehad just completed his Rite of[Passag] wh [e] n | arrived. | don’t know what kind of names the Fidnna use, but he still uses his human name.” She sighed,eyes. Many and shook ofthem her do head,in Wales, “He carries| found.” his uncle's klaive| but does not boast. He has the strangest The spirit hopped from one foot to the other. “What do you feel for him?” “| don't know, friend cuckoo. He is Garou, soeven if|did wish to takea mate, it could neverbe him. Buthehadan honesty inhis manner, in hideyesshnch have seenonlyin spirits. Asthough he knew...” she trailed of£ tryingto find what she meantto say. She reflected that Aneurin himself ironically enoush, would probably know exactly howto express himself: “As though he knew himself” “Ah.” The cuckoo-spiritwas obviously displeased. Although the bird looked harmless, it was brave and powerful, and itanswered Brecthfte Great Fenris. “Will you see him again?” “How would | know that?” Yvonne asked, confused. “You are a Crescent Moon, What does your soul say?” Yvonne looked up, and saw the crescent moon — Aneurin’s moon and hers — shining down. ‘I think somehow The | will. Gaia help me.” f i ’ cuckoo fluttered to her shoulder and pecked sharply at her ear. “Gaia says help yourself, daughter of Fenris. Now, wake that ax as you promised, and no more wasted breaths.” The bird puffeditselfup as Yvonne knelt again and began the rite. “Besides, ifyou do see him again, I'm sureit will be for agood reason.” The Theurge glanced toward the bird, who promptly pecked at her cheek. “Pay attention to your work.”

    The physical prowess of werewolves is legendary, but the magical powers they wield gain them even greater advantage in the harsh world of rhe Dark Medieval. Gifts from the spirits and the rituals that keep alive their heritage are just as integral to the Garou as any amount of martial skill. This chapter details the Gifts and rites that the werewolves use in their fight against the Wyrm (and, occasionally, each other).

    PRA GlANceEdBACK at the MEN Flanking beg. She had never been good at talking her way out of trouble, especially where men were concerned. She probably should have skipped the village altogether, wandered in the nearby fields in wolf form-and. caught her dinner that way, but she hadn't been among humans in months.     And what rough beast, tts hour come round at last, Slouches toward Bethlehem to be born? —Wiilliam Butler Yeats, “The Second Coming”

    Novice or veteran, your storytelling goals are likely the same. You want to tell a tale that your players will delight in now and tell stories about for years to come. Asa Storyteller, it is a tremendous compliment to hear your players reminisce about a surprising plot twist, a touching scene of an enemy whose name or theme music always makes them shiver. This chapter provides some tips on crafting Dark Ages: Werewolf chronicles. The Dark Medieval can be difficult to get your mind around. With a lot of thought and a little planning, you could have an epic saga on your hands and players who are champing at the bit to find out what happens next.
